        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1310928824" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11358818737473782420">This book was useful with regard to learning some of the history and lore of DA, but the writing was atrocious. Like totally ridiculous. All telling and little showing. Out of place phrases. And convoluted sentence structure. This book could have done with massive editing. Sometimes the characters behaved in completely unrealistic unnatural ways and made childish decisions. I'm conflicted about this book. The I formation was good and thus it served it's purpose for me, but the poor writing zappe</span>
  <span id="freeText11358818737473782420" style="display:none">This book was useful with regard to learning some of the history and lore of DA, but the writing was atrocious. Like totally ridiculous. All telling and little showing. Out of place phrases. And convoluted sentence structure. This book could have done with massive editing. Sometimes the characters behaved in completely unrealistic unnatural ways and made childish decisions. I'm conflicted about this book. The I formation was good and thus it served it's purpose for me, but the poor writing zapped all the juice.</span>

<div id="review_1765526305" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1765526305" />
    <a title="n ❀" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39437300-n"><img alt="n ❀" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540099209p2/39437300.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1765526305?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="n ❀" class="user" itemprop="url" name="n ❀" href="/user/show/39437300-n">n ❀</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1765526305&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1765526305" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10983006881496514914">i can't believe that david gaider - lead writer of dragonage - WROTE THIS PIECE OF SHIT. i honestly have never read anything like this before. he made a fan fiction of his own masterpiece, but that's not all.<br/><br/>if you can't tell, i'm a huge fan of dragonage origins. there would be no other reason for me to pick this up unless i thought otherwise. i actually bought <i>the calling</i> and <i>asunder</i> long before i bought <i>stolen throne</i>, but i decided to go in order despite my undying love for duncan. before i go</span>
  <span id="freeText10983006881496514914" style="display:none">i can't believe that david gaider - lead writer of dragonage - WROTE THIS PIECE OF SHIT. i honestly have never read anything like this before. he made a fan fiction of his own masterpiece, but that's not all.<br /><br />if you can't tell, i'm a huge fan of dragonage origins. there would be no other reason for me to pick this up unless i thought otherwise. i actually bought <i>the calling</i> and <i>asunder</i> long before i bought <i>stolen throne</i>, but i decided to go in order despite my undying love for duncan. before i go completely off topic, maybe i'll start with a small synopsis so we all get warmed up to this blasphemy.<br /><br />maric is the son of rebel queen moira. with an orlesian occupied ferelden, the heir of royalty watches his mother handle armies of men that abide by her commands. when the local bann's turn their backs on her and her son, the rebel queen is slain by orlesian forces, leaving maric to flee. barely making it out of the forest alive, maric meets a young outlaw named loghain who helps him to a camp of surviving bandits (or just mere survivors if we're getting into it). later revealed that this particular blonde haired boy is none other than rebel prince maric theirin. after a few turning events, maric begins on his plight to avenge his fallen mother with loghain at his side, a woman named rowan promised to him as queen, and a strange elf with a dark secret named katriel. under the maker's gaze and for ferelden will orlais tremble before the rebel army.<br /><br />now! <br /><br />i made it sound pretty bad ass, haven't i? that's pretty much what i thought of when first seeing this beauty. alas, i was proven wrong as the chapters slowly moved by. david gaider writers with far too much detail. he wants you to see what he see's, but doesn't know how to simplify anything. he blows things up by over complicating them, and he can't stop but pull at cliche's from left to right. here's a small list.<br /><br />- maric is the son of rebel queen moira, but somehow managed to live a privileged and sheltered life given that he was in orlesian occupied ferelden with men trying to hunt down the royal bloodline. this makes up for an overly naive character for ALL of the story (i shit you not) who puts his own wants before his people and in the span of three years just can't get his head out of his ass<br /><br />- katriel is an elf who falls upon the rebel's by chance. though there's a passage that talks about an unknown elf spy (bard), it's safe to say gaider doesn't know how to keep his readers in suspense and goes for star-crossed bullshit. katriel - who does some horrible things - manages to infiltrate the rebel's, screw them over, and stay till the end. she also reminds me of a combination of morrigan and zevran from dragonage: origins, both of whom i hate to the core of my existence and their know-it-all, oversexualized bitchiness. though katriel is just a know-it-all bitch, it's safe to say i hated her the most<br /><br />- rowan is the headstrong daughter of an arl whose two younger brothers are eamon and teagan sent to the free marches. serving as part of the rebel army from a commander's perspective, she's what i call the "typical girl" that every book has. she's headstrong and can battle against the orlesian's yet come out looking pretty attractive...though i don't even know how that's possible. she's physically stronger in battle than almost every man and can also show dominance over maric without even trying. basically she's like a bro without the hunking muscles, backwards cap, and instagram selfies that say "#beastmode" <br /><br />- love cliche's! katriel falls for maric, maric falls for katriel. rowan loves maric and loghain, but loghain has feelings for rowan and doesn't embrace them until they're trapped in the deep roads (oh yea! they're trapped in the deep roads for like four chaps!) <br /><br />- maric kills katriel because her betrayal is finally uncovered. this is when he decides to go to the dark side. because that's what happens, you know? you find out the person you're in love with in WAR is actually an orlesian bard whose been sent to screw up your charges and is the reason why you almost lost. so then you have to kill them because you're technically the rightful king of ferelden and, oh, you still have a call-girl named rowan to make your queen. so why not?<br /><br />i know, i know. if i hate this piece of shit so much, why the hell did i give it two stars? well, i'll tell you. while the majority of this book was full of useless detailing, which, if i took out would probably cut the book in half from it's whooping 400+ pages, it had it's moments near the end. there was a coming together of politics and pride. i wanted to see this long before. you have to keep in mind that the story takes its course over three years and there isn't character development until loghain unveils katriel as the little snake she is. this is partly why <i>the stolen throne</i> had a last minute bump-up from the one-star crap i believed it was. <br /><br />i will say, like the norm, my favorite character was loghain mac tir who you see for the ice-cold warrior he is. the loving moments he shares with maric proves that he wasn't what we've seen in dragonage: origins. in the game, he's the ultimate antagonist who wants to rule with an iron fist. i'll give credit where credit is due, gaider does well in portraying this man and you find out why he feels justified as to the crimes he commits as teyrn of gwaren in origins. you see his hatred for elves that come at the price of perhaps what katriel had done, how she had so sneakily heed loyalty to the orlesian charges over her own. you see his hatred for orlais and why he refuses the orlesian wardens for wanting to come in and help (and also why he let duncan die). <br /><br />you also see the friendship between loghain and maric change by the end. you see maric become what you wanted to see, given that blackness has tainted his heart. it's a shame that gaider didn't show this brand of change earlier. because in my head, i always saw maric as the type of ruthless, strong-minded, stubborn, iron-clad king that he was supposed to be. wearing gold armor with his blonde hair cascading down his back, he'd have a scowl on his face, a few scars received in battle...just the whole nine yards. instead, i got maric. you know? an alistair in the middle of war. and let me just say, it doesn't look good. especially if maric only goes bat shit crazy and changes because his first love was an blonde haired elf bard that had quite a weird relationship with him. but who am i to judge about love? this is, after all, the most bullshit book i've read, now haven't i?<br /><br />alas if you're wondering, as it is in the games, rowan marries maric and the two do manage to work to fall in love. they have cailan, the idiot we see in the game, and unfortunately, the queen dies long before she can see him grow into said idiot. <br /><br />as a die hard fan of dragonage, i have to say i lost some "kazaam!" for david gaider. actually, that's a lie. i lost respect and what not from him when he created characters like zevran or dorian or whatever stereotypical gay character he could. what he did for <i>the stolen throne</i> was put all these over hyped elements together that came together in a sloppy fashion. <br /><br />and don't worry! i'll take a fall for the love of the maker and read up on his two other books only to shit on them the way i had this one. adieu </span>
  <a data-text-id="10983006881496514914" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1242305645" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1242305645" />
    <a title="Nerine Dorman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1611208-nerine-dorman"><img alt="Nerine Dorman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572964607p2/1611208.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1242305645?book_show_action=true">Mar 31, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nerine Dorman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nerine Dorman" href="/user/show/1611208-nerine-dorman">Nerine Dorman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1242305645" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1212936757549784692">Anyone who knows me well will know that I’ve an insatiable appetite for lore. They’ll also know that I’m an incorrigible addict when it comes to fantasy that involves dragons, elves and magic. So needless to say, now that I’ve fallen into the black hole that is BioWare’s Dragon Age franchise, there is no hope for this Middle-earth veteran.<br/><br/>My main motivation for picking up The Stolen Throne *was* for the lore, as well as the backstory for characters and events. When you’re looking at a setting th</span>
  <span id="freeText1212936757549784692" style="display:none">Anyone who knows me well will know that I’ve an insatiable appetite for lore. They’ll also know that I’m an incorrigible addict when it comes to fantasy that involves dragons, elves and magic. So needless to say, now that I’ve fallen into the black hole that is BioWare’s Dragon Age franchise, there is no hope for this Middle-earth veteran.<br /><br />My main motivation for picking up The Stolen Throne *was* for the lore, as well as the backstory for characters and events. When you’re looking at a setting that’s so magnificently portrayed in the gaming environment, as well as an environment that has spawned so much fan-created artistic and literary content, you’re really onto something special. At least for the fans, that is.<br /><br />Which is why The Stolen Throne was great. The story is simple. Prince Maric’s on the run after his mother, the queen, is murdered thanks to the treachery of her subjects. The Fereldan kingdom is ruled by an usurper placed on the throne by the neighbouring Empire of Orlesia, and Maric faces a bitter struggle before he can take his rightful place as ruler and gain vengeance. Helping him are his betrothed, Rowan, and his loyal and best friend Loghain, who stand by him through all his battles. <br /><br />For those who played through Dragon Age: Origins, Maric is Alistair’s grandfather, so it’s a nice touch to see this little slice of history brought to life, and especially getting an idea of the socio-political setting for the magnificent world of Thedas.<br /><br />But…<br /><br />Yes. You knew there was going to be a but, didn’t you…<br /><br />The execution of this novel didn’t blow me away. While I appreciated the content, its delivery could have been better, and this is where I am not afraid to say that a savvy content editor would have been able to poke and prod the author to give a little more. The plot itself is fine – and suitably unpredictable. I certainly did not expect a diversion down into the [spoiler] where the inevitable [spoilers] were encountered. And oh, look, cool loot! I sometimes felt that character's’ motivations could have been given a bit more voema. The dialogue could have been a bit more complex. The environment could have been gifted with more sensual experience. Lots of could haves… If the characters are in a forest, I want to smell the leaf mould, feel the coolness of the air… That sort of thing. I wanted to be struck by the sheer magnificence of the setting the way I am when I play through Dragon Age: Inquisition. <br /><br />So, yeah, it fell a little flat for me. <br /><br />Overall, this one hovers a little between three and four stars for me. There were times when my heart quickened (because I had my favourite characters, like Rowan and Katriel, who are both strong women with agency in a hostile environment). But there were often times when I felt the prose didn’t live up to its potential. Will I go on to reading others in the series. Yes. Because I’m a sucker for canon and I’m a total geek hoping to be able to map out details for when I’m playing the game or writing fics. So, this is one for the die-hard fans. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1212936757549784692" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_167553303" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/167553303" />
    <a title="Jason" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4628717-jason"><img alt="Jason" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1297614333p2/4628717.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/167553303?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason" href="/user/show/4628717-jason">Jason</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4628717-jason?shelf=medieval-fantasy">medieval-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer167553303" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11595363613368278939">If you enjoyed the Dragon Age series of games, this is an acceptable read. It provides a back story to the kingdom of Feredlen, and little more. There were a few good moments, and I did think a bit about a couple of the characters after concluding the book, but overall I can't recommend it to anyone who isn't just thirsting for more Dragon Age story.<br/><br/>As the lead writer for Origins, the Stolen Throne reads just like the game. I can see Maric choosing the 'witty' dialogue choice throughout the book</span>
  <span id="freeText11595363613368278939" style="display:none">If you enjoyed the Dragon Age series of games, this is an acceptable read. It provides a back story to the kingdom of Feredlen, and little more. There were a few good moments, and I did think a bit about a couple of the characters after concluding the book, but overall I can't recommend it to anyone who isn't just thirsting for more Dragon Age story.<br /><br />As the lead writer for Origins, the Stolen Throne reads just like the game. I can see Maric choosing the 'witty' dialogue choice throughout the book. He sounds just like Alistair with his self-deprecating humor (whom I always thought sounded a bit like Ricky Gervais in style). Likewise, Loghain consistently chooses the 'severe' dialogue choice. <br /><br />The writing could use some polish, and Gaider could learn a few more metaphors and expressions outside what he wrote into the games. Maric does evolve as a character, much like Alistair is 'hardened' in the game. Loghain is barely likable enough to tolerate through the book, though one wonders why Maric does. Maric's elven lover tries to evolve as a character, but doesn't seem to quite make it. The remainder of the cast experiences change by being skewered by a sword, or remains a static prop.<br /><br />For fantasy, it isn't very fantastic. It's pretty mundane medieval with a sprinkling of elves and dwarves. A couple of wizards show up to fight and provide fingerprint services. One dragon makes a brief metaphorical appearance. And one scene with dark spawn. And there's a magic sword. That's the sum of fantasy.<br /><br />For the Dragon Age fans: Not much in world creation. A few towns are introduced, and some background nobility are introduced and then summarily killed off. There's some side discussion of Orlesian culture. There's an obligatory walk through the Deep Roads.<br /><br />And in the tradition of Tolkien, there's absolutely no scale to the Kingdom of Ferelden. Some times it takes a month to travel across, other times it can be traversed in an afternoon. Why can't the customary map ever have a bar scale?<br /><br />As a fan of the Dragon Age series, and all the encyclopedic information revealed through the games, I had high hopes for this read. However, except for a scene or two, it was largely forgettable. It felt rushed, especially at the end, and a lot of story telling opportunities and possible plot twists were missed or not fully explored. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11595363613368278939" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_86696304" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/86696304" />
    <a title="Dennis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/203037-dennis"><img alt="Dennis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1199781338p2/203037.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/86696304?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dennis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dennis" href="/user/show/203037-dennis">Dennis</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer86696304" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11424254162732685651">It's not awful, but it's definitely not good. The first chapter consists almost entirely of straight-up description. The rest is littered with anachronistic cliches, typos (e.g. "you're" for "your". Seriously!), redundant description, poor word choices, and weak metaphors.<br/><br/>Everything about the book is on-the-nose. The reader is left with nothing to ponder or imagine.<br/><br/>What's good? The plot, I guess. It's a prelude novel to the Dragon Age video game, by the lead writer, David Gaider. Bioware should </span>
  <span id="freeText11424254162732685651" style="display:none">It's not awful, but it's definitely not good. The first chapter consists almost entirely of straight-up description. The rest is littered with anachronistic cliches, typos (e.g. "you're" for "your". Seriously!), redundant description, poor word choices, and weak metaphors.<br /><br />Everything about the book is on-the-nose. The reader is left with nothing to ponder or imagine.<br /><br />What's good? The plot, I guess. It's a prelude novel to the Dragon Age video game, by the lead writer, David Gaider. Bioware should really have hired a ghostwriter, or at least a competent editor. There's no reason a novel based on a video game can't be good. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11424254162732685651" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

Anyway, liked this a lot better than Asunder and some day I look forward to reading the other books. <br/>Sure, some times it was slow and a bit repetetive (I probably wrote that wrong) but all in all, a good story. Enjoyable.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1141798010" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17592471654938292138">While there weren't any big surprises or twists, this was an interesting story well-told. I appreciated the additional background for Loghain, but found it a little difficult to reconcile the book's sympathetic version with the video game's harsher presentation. It has been some time since I played the game, however, perhaps my memory is faulty. I look forward to reading David Gaider's subsequent Dragon Age novels.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Ci/LvaTnSO65rdPOApZU/PO31IOYN7A3cn/szzu+eRY5obGhihGw0ODfKnGq1eij4dwl2GP3vCr4N+a+pEAXaA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZpwUUiABksU4PHJx1NPLyzEHj5OlbJKp5BCVs13iTexVEm5ODvdq+2FOi858kHeUI2x+yF6snrRuWJ/Cwhwjkg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/2834177.David_Gaider">About David Gaider</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/2834177.David_Gaider"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1454638220p3/2834177.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/2834177.David_Gaider">David Gaider
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
494
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9947508237025599430">David Gaider lives in Edmonton, Alberta, and has worked for video game developer BioWare since 1999. He is the lead writer on the upcoming Dragon Age: Origins role-playing game and has previously worked on such titles as Baldur’s Gate 2: Shadows of Amn, Star Wars: Knights of the Old Republic, and Neverwinter Nights.</span>

</div>
